Current top1 is neutral aromatic (restriction-of-intramolecular-motion dominated AIE typical of multi-phenyl rotor systems). Current top2 is ICT (donor–acceptor substituted π-system may have charge-transfer S1 character). Top1 is only a working hypothesis because the structure also contains plausible donor (OMe) / acceptor (CHO) groups and substantial torsional freedom, which can shift the excited state toward ICT or even a solvent-stabilized TICT minimum. Key uncertainty between neutral aromatic vs ICT/TICT is whether S1 is primarily locally excited (LE) on the π-framework (small electron–hole separation, modest dipole change) or charge-transfer (larger dipole, spatially separated NTOs), and whether twisting leads to a low-oscillator-strength TICT-like state in solution. Shared prepared structure context is available and ready (10 conformers generated; selected conformer_id=8; prepared XYZ/SDF paths provided). Macro can provide structural/photophysical plausibility arguments (rotors, planarity proxy, donor/acceptor pattern) but cannot conclusively diagnose excited-state character. Microscopic can provide a bounded baseline S0 optimization + S1 vertical excitation on the shared structure to extract excitation energy, oscillator strength, orbital/NTO localization and dipole-change proxies—directly informative for distinguishing LE (neutral aromatic) vs CT (ICT/TICT). First round should gather both: macro to frame the mechanism candidates and microscopic to obtain first-principles evidence about S1 character at low cost.

- reasoning_summary: From the shared prepared structure context, the molecule is a neutral (charge 0, singlet) multi-aryl, rotor-rich scaffold: 5 aromatic rings (5 ring systems), 8 rotatable bonds, and 11 branch points. This topology is consistent with a neutral aromatic chromophore where intramolecular rotations can be restricted (RIM/RIR plausibility) rather than an intrinsically ionic/zwitterionic dye. The hetero-atom content is low (3 hetero atoms total) and corresponds to two methoxy substituents (electron-donating) and one aldehyde (electron-withdrawing), yielding a donor/acceptor substitution pattern that could introduce some ICT character; however, within current macro scope we can only flag this as a structural possibility, not resolve it. Geometry proxies from the selected conformer indicate high planarity_proxy (~0.95) and high compactness_proxy (~0.93), suggesting an extended but relatively planar/compact π-framework in that conformer, while the presence of multiple rotatable aryl–alkene/aryl–aryl connections still supports torsional degrees of freedom (torsion_candidate_count = 8). Overall, the macro structural indicators support the "neutral aromatic" working hypothesis (neutral, multi-aryl conjugation), while noting a built-in donor–acceptor motif (OMe vs CHO) that could enable CT-like excited states that cannot be confirmed/ruled out here.
Capability limit note: This macro step is limited to deterministic single-molecule structural/topological evidence and provided geometry proxies. It cannot compute or infer excited-state properties, quantify ICT/TICT vs LE, or evaluate aggregation/packing effects; it can only flag structural prerequisites/risks (neutrality, aromaticity, rotors, donor/acceptor substitution).

### Round 1 | planner | planner_diagnosis

Latest microscopic baseline neither decisively strengthens nor weakens neutral-aromatic vs ICT: the lowest excited state is bright with sizable oscillator strength (S1: 3.203 eV, f=0.438), which is compatible with a locally allowed π–π* transition but is not diagnostic for/against ICT without CT descriptors. Reasoning summary: From the shared prepared structure context, the molecule is a neutral (charge 0, singlet) multi-aryl, rotor-rich scaffold: 5 aromatic rings (5 ring systems), 8 rotatable bonds, and 11 branch points. This topology is consistent with a neutral aromatic chromophore where intramolecular rotations can be restricted (RIM/RIR plausibility) rather than an intrinsically ionic/zwitterionic dye. The hetero-atom content is low (3 hetero atoms total) and corresponds to two methoxy substituents (electron-donating) and one aldehyde (electron-withdrawing), yielding a donor/acceptor substitution pattern that could introduce some ICT character; however, within current macro scope we can only flag this as a structural possibility, not resolve it. Geometry proxies from the selected conformer indicate high planarity_proxy (~0.95) and high compactness_proxy (~0.93), suggesting an extended but relatively planar/compact π-framework in that conformer, while the presence of multiple rotatable aryl–alkene/aryl–aryl connections still supports torsional degrees of freedom (torsion_candidate_count = 8). Overall, the macro structural indicators support the "neutral aromatic" working hypothesis (neutral, multi-aryl conjugation), while noting a built-in donor–acceptor motif (OMe vs CHO) that could enable CT-like excited states that cannot be confirmed/ruled out here.
Capability limit note: This macro step is limited to deterministic single-molecule structural/topological evidence and provided geometry proxies. It cannot compute or infer excited-state properties, quantify ICT/TICT vs LE, or evaluate aggregation/packing effects; it can only flag structural prerequisites/risks (neutrality, aromaticity, rotors, donor/acceptor substitution).

### Round 3 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 3/20 (18 remaining). Top-1 is neutral aromatic (0.41) vs top-2 ICT (0.27). Latest microscopic follow-up (run_targeted_state_characterization) strengthens neutral-aromatic slightly by confirming: (i) S1 remains the lowest and strongly bright state (E≈3.203 eV, f≈0.438) with a dominant single transition (131→132, |c|≈0.70), and (ii) a nearby dark S2 exists (E≈3.307 eV, f=0), but without CT descriptors we cannot assign S2 as CT vs symmetry-forbidden LE. The latest evidence does not directly confirm ICT because the requested CT discriminators (NTO localization, electron–hole separation/overlap, CT number) are still missing even after a generation-capable attempt; thus ICT is slightly weakened relative to neutral-aromatic. An additional candidate affected is TICT: presence of many torsions + a nearby dark state keeps TICT as a hedge, but still lacks torsion/geometry dependence evidence.
Key remaining discriminator between neutral aromatic and ICT: direct excited-state charge-separation diagnostics (NTO hole/electron localization on donor vs acceptor rings; e–h centroid distance; overlap/CT-number; ideally Δμ or solvatochromic sensitivity). Verifier supplementation status is still missing. Closure justification is now effectively blocked internally for this pair because two internal routes (parse-only extraction and targeted characterization) have failed to produce the needed CT observables. Therefore the best next action is Verifier: seek external precedents/diagnostic criteria for this specific scaffold class (multi-aryl/triarylethene-like with OMe/CHO) to discriminate LE/RIM-dominated emission vs ICT-dominated emission when explicit CT descriptors are unavailable.

- action: verifier

- confidence: 0.41

(2) diagnostic patterns: if S1 is lowest and bright with high oscillator strength, does literature typically interpret this as LE rather than ICT for such scaffolds? (3) whether presence of a nearby dark S2 in D–A aryl systems is commonly CT-like or can be symmetry/geometry-driven LE. Return concise criteria and any comparable compounds; explicitly state what would challenge the current top-1 (neutral aromatic) vs support ICT.

(2) diagnostic patterns: if S1 is lowest and bright with high oscillator strength, does literature typically interpret this as LE rather than ICT for such scaffolds? - diagnosis: Round 5/20 (16 rounds remaining). Top-1 remains neutral aromatic (0.29) with ICT extremely close (0.28); TICT (0.19) and unknown (0.22) are now more competitive. Latest evidence (microscopic torsion snapshots on a high-relevance aryl–vinyl dihedral) weakens the earlier ‘robust bright lowest S1’ picture: in the torsion run, the lowest vertical state is dark (f≈0) and the first bright state appears higher (pattern: lowest_state_is_dark_then_bright). This geometry-sensitivity and emergence of a low-lying dark state increases compatibility with ICT/TICT-type state mixing, or at minimum challenges a simple LE-only assignment. However, the current torsion output summary is incomplete for closure because we do not yet have the full per-snapshot (states 1–3) energy/f tables across all 6 angles to confirm whether there is state crossing/reordering or whether the dark state persists at all angles. Key remaining discriminator for neutral aromatic vs ICT is still direct CT evidence (CT-number/hole–electron separation/Δμ or solvatochromism); given internal CT-descriptor export is blocked, the best available internal discriminator is now torsion-dependent state ordering/brightness trends—requiring full parsing of the torsion snapshot bundle. Verifier supplementation is sufficient/high-IG but mixed; closure justification is still collecting (internal) and not yet sufficient. Next action is best now: parse the torsion snapshot bundle to extract the per-snapshot per-state table needed for a discriminative LE/ICT/TICT interpretation.

### Round 6 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 6/20 (15 remaining). Top-1 is now ICT (0.34) vs top-2 neutral aromatic (0.24), with unknown (0.22) close behind.

Latest evidence (parsed torsion snapshots, states 1–3 across 0/15/30/45/60/90° for a high-relevance aryl–vinyl dihedral) strengthens the challenger picture against a robust LE-bright lowest state: at every torsion angle the lowest state is (near-)dark (S1 f≈0–0.0008), while the first bright state is consistently S2 (f rises from 0.064 at 0° to 0.185 at 90°). S1 energy increases from 3.2447→3.8831 eV with twisting; S2 increases from 3.9569→4.5225 eV, and S2 oscillator strength increases markedly. This pattern makes a neutral-aromatic/LE interpretation less likely as the *dominant lowest-state picture* and is compatible with a low-lying dark CT-mixed (ICT-like) or otherwise dark state competing with a higher bright LE state.

Effect on top2: neutral aromatic is weakened because the emitting manifold is not robustly 'lowest bright'; instead, the system shows persistent low-lying dark-state behavior under a conjugation-relevant torsion.

Effect on an additional candidate: TICT is moderated—torsion sensitivity exists, but there is no torsion-driven crossing where a twisted geometry stabilizes a lower CT state relative to the bright state; instead both S1 and S2 energies rise with twist.

Key remaining discriminator between ICT vs neutral aromatic: whether the dark S1 is genuinely charge-transfer (hole on OMe-donor side, electron on CHO-acceptor side; CT-number/Δμ/solvatochromism) versus a non-CT dark state (e.g., n→π* from the aldehyde or a symmetry/selection-rule forbidden LE state). Verifier supplementation is sufficient (high IG, mixed), but internal closure is still collecting because we lack direct CT descriptors.

Chosen next action rationale: run a conformer sensitivity screen (bounded) to test whether the 'lowest dark / S2 bright' ordering is robust across realistic conformers (supports an intrinsic low-lying dark state consistent with ICT competition) or is specific to a particular torsional setting (would keep neutral aromatic/unknown more competitive).

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.34

- task_instruction: Microscopic (single registry action): run_conformer_bundle. Generate a small conformer set (e.g., max_conformers=6; reuse existing prepared structure if supported). For each conformer, compute vertical excited states 1–3 and report excitation_energy_ev and oscillator_strength for each state plus the per-conformer pattern: whether the lowest-energy state is bright or dark and the index/energy of the first bright state. Goal: quantify how often the system shows 'lowest dark then bright' (as in the torsion scan) versus 'lowest bright' across conformers.

### Round 7 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 7/20 with 14 rounds remaining. Reweighting shifts top-1 to neutral aromatic (0.33) over ICT (0.27). Latest evidence (bounded conformer bundle, 6 conformers) shows the lowest excited state is consistently bright (pattern=lowest_state_is_bright; S1 f~0.44; very small excitation-energy spread ~0.03 eV), which weakens the previous ICT-favored interpretation based on the torsion-snapshot series where S1 was persistently dark and S2 was the first bright state. Thus: (i) the latest evidence weakens ICT as a globally dominant label, (ii) it strengthens the neutral-aromatic/LE picture for relaxed conformers, and (iii) it increases pressure on an 'unknown/borderline' hedge because the torsion-snapshot dark-state behavior may be specific to forced geometries or a particular dihedral range not represented in the conformer set. Key remaining discriminator between top-1 and top-2: whether the dark low-lying state seen in torsion snapshots is (a) genuinely CT/ICT in character and thermally accessible (supporting ICT/TICT) or (b) a symmetry/selection-rule/n→π* or otherwise non-CT dark state appearing under constrained twisting (supporting neutral aromatic with RIM and occasional dark-state access). Verifier supplementation remains sufficient/high-gain but mixed (close-family evidence supports both LE/RIM and D–A ICT regimes). Closure justification remains collecting; next best step is to extract the full per-conformer state (1–3) tables from the conformer bundle to see if any conformer reproduces the 'lowest dark then bright' ordering and to compare state ordering/brightness patterns across the ensemble.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.33

- task_instruction: Microscopic (single registry action): parse_snapshot_outputs. Reuse artifact_bundle_id='round_07_conformer_bundle'. Extract a structured per-conformer table for each conformer member (all 6): states 1–3 with excitation_energy_ev and oscillator_strength, plus a derived label per conformer of whether the lowest-energy state is bright or dark and the index/energy of the first bright state. Goal: check whether any relaxed conformer shows the 'lowest_state_is_dark_then_bright' pattern seen in torsion snapshots, or whether 'lowest_state_is_bright' is robust across conformers. Return only parsed observables + limitations; no global mechanism judgment.

- hypothesis_uncertainty_note: Internal evidence is currently bifurcated: (a) forced torsion snapshots show a persistent dark lowest state across angles for one aryl–vinyl dihedral, while (b) relaxed conformer sampling shows a consistently bright lowest state with minimal spread. Without CT-number/NTO/Δμ or solvatochromism, the electronic character and mechanistic role of the dark state cannot be assigned confidently, leaving ICT vs neutral-aromatic vs mixed (unknown) unresolved.

- final_hypothesis_rationale: null

Verifier supplementation is already sufficient/high-gain but remains close-family and mixed (no exact-compound hit).

### Round 8 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 8/20 (13 remaining). Top-1 is neutral aromatic (0.40) and top-2 is unknown (0.22), with ICT close (0.20).

Latest evidence strengthens the prior neutral-aromatic (LE/RIM-compatible) picture: parsing the conformer bundle shows all 6 relaxed conformers have the same qualitative ordering/pattern: S1 is the lowest state and is strongly bright (f≈0.44–0.47), with very small excitation-energy dispersion. This undermines the hypothesis that the lowest state is generically dark/CT-like across thermally accessible geometries.

Effect on the ICT challenger: ICT is weakened because the bright lowest state is robust across conformers, and the available transition proxy (dominant single HOMO→LUMO-like excitation for S1) is more consistent with an LE-like state than a strongly charge-separated CT state. However, ICT cannot be ruled out because donor–acceptor substitution and close-family literature still allow partial/borderline ICT without direct CT-number/NTO/Δμ or solvatochromism.

Effect on an additional candidate (TICT): TICT remains possible because the forced torsion route previously produced a dark lowest state, but its relevance is questionable because those snapshots were not ground-state optimized; TICT is therefore kept as a secondary geometry-sensitive mechanism rather than the dominant assignment.

Key remaining discriminator: whether the torsion-snapshot “dark S1” persists when each torsion snapshot is made physically realistic (i.e., with per-snapshot S0 optimization under the dihedral constraint). If the dark-lowest-state pattern disappears upon S0 optimization, it likely reflects an artifact of high-strain, non-equilibrium geometries rather than a mechanistically relevant CT/TICT state.

Verifier supplementation: sufficient and high-information but mixed (close-family supports both LE/RIM and D–A ICT regimes; exact-compound evidence is missing).

Closure justification: still collecting; we now have robust per-conformer state tables, but we still need to reconcile them with the torsion-snapshot result using a more realistic torsion protocol.

Why next action is best now: rerunning torsion snapshots with ground-state optimization (still a single bounded registry action) directly tests whether the earlier dark-lowest-state finding is robust or a non-optimized-geometry artifact, which is the most discriminative remaining internal step for neutral aromatic vs ICT/TICT/unknown.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.4

- task_instruction: Microscopic (single registry action): run_torsion_snapshots with ground-state optimization enabled to test whether the previously observed low-lying dark S1 is an artifact of non-optimized strained snapshots. Use the same high-relevance aryl–vinyl dihedral as before (dihedral_id=dih_0_1_2_3; atoms [0,1,2,3]). Settings: optimize_ground_state=true; snapshot_count=4; target_angle_deg grid = [0, 30, 60, 90] (or equivalent angle_offsets). Compute vertical states 1–3 per snapshot. Report per-snapshot state 1–3 excitation_energy_ev and oscillator_strength and the derived lowest_state_to_brightest_pattern (lowest bright vs lowest dark then bright). Return raw tables + limitations only (no global mechanism judgment).

- hypothesis_uncertainty_note: Although relaxed conformers robustly show a bright lowest S1, forced torsion snapshots previously produced a persistent dark lowest state. Because the torsion snapshots were run without S0 optimization, it is unclear whether that dark state is physically relevant (thermally accessible) or an artifact of strained, non-equilibrium geometries. Direct CT diagnostics (NTO localization/CT-number/e–h separation/Δμ) and experimental solvatochromism remain unavailable, limiting decisive LE vs ICT attribution.

- final_hypothesis_rationale: null

- capability_assessment: Microscopic: strong at generating/paring vertical manifolds across conformers and torsion snapshots and extracting state energies/oscillator strengths and dominant-transition proxies. Repeated limitation: available low-cost routes do not reliably export decisive CT diagnostics (NTO localization, CT-number, electron–hole separation/overlap, Δμ). Verifier: provided sufficient close-family context but no exact-compound hit; emphasizes solvatochromism/CT-number as decisive but those observables are missing here.

### Round 9 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 9/20 (12 rounds remaining). Top-1 is neutral aromatic (0.55) and top-2 is ICT (0.20); unknown is now third (0.15).

Latest evidence strengthens the current top-1: the new torsion snapshots were rerun with ground-state optimization enabled (optimize_ground_state=true) on the same high-relevance aryl–vinyl dihedral (dih_0_1_2_3). Unlike the earlier non-optimized torsion series that produced a persistent dark lowest state, the optimized torsion series shows the lowest state is bright (lowest_state_is_bright) across 0/30/60/90°, and torsion sensitivity is essentially absent. This strongly suggests the earlier dark-state pattern was an artifact of strained/non-equilibrium geometries rather than a physically relevant competing low-lying dark state.

Effect on challengers: (i) ICT is weakened because the main internal discriminator that previously favored CT-like competition (a robust dark lowest state under twisting) disappears under physically more plausible torsion snapshots; however, ICT remains plausible structurally and from close-family literature, pending CT-number/NTO/Δμ/solvatochromism. (ii) Unknown is reduced because the key inconsistency driving it has largely been resolved.

Key remaining discriminator between neutral aromatic and ICT: direct excited-state charge-separation diagnostics (CT-number / hole–electron separation/overlap / Δμ) or experimental solvatochromism; we still only have energies/oscillator strengths and dominant-transition proxies.

Verifier supplementation status: sufficient (mixed close-family precedent), but no longer the bottleneck.
Closure justification status: still collecting; we should finish extracting a complete per-snapshot (states 1–3) table from the new optimized torsion bundle to confirm there is no low-lying dark state across angles in the full 1–3 manifold.

Chosen next action rationale: a low-cost parse of the new optimized torsion snapshot bundle is the most discriminative and immediate step to complete pairwise closure (neutral aromatic vs ICT) using already-generated artifacts, without repeating stalled CT-descriptor export routes.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.55

### Round 10 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 10/20 (11 rounds remaining). Top-1 is neutral aromatic (0.72) vs top-2 ICT (0.14).

Latest evidence strengthens the current top-1 and weakens the top-2: parsing the S0-optimized torsion snapshot bundle (round_09_torsion_snapshots; 0/30/60/90° on dihedral [0,1,2,3]) shows the ordering/brightness is stable across angles with state_ordering pattern = lowest_state_is_bright for every snapshot. Numerically, S1 remains bright (f≈0.4308–0.4393) and nearly angle-invariant (ΔE≈0.0008 eV; Δf≈0.0085). S2 is consistently dark/nearly dark (f≈0–0.0001) and sits ~0.10 eV above S1 (e.g., at 90°: S1 3.2028 eV f=0.4308; S2 3.3121 eV f=0.0001; S3 3.8481 eV f=0.201). Dominant transitions remain consistent with an LE-like HOMO→LUMO excitation for S1.

Effect on top-2 (ICT): while D–A substitution and close-family literature keep ICT plausible, the internal geometric-robustness tests now strongly favor a robust bright lowest S1 rather than a competing low-lying dark CT-like state; the prior dark-S1 torsion evidence is now best explained as a non-optimized (strained) snapshot artifact.

Key remaining discriminator between neutral aromatic and ICT: direct CT diagnostics (CT-number/NTO hole–electron separation/overlap, Δμ) and/or experimental solvatochromism. However, given the robust bright S1 across both conformers and S0-optimized torsion snapshots, the best-available assignment favors neutral aromatic.

Verifier supplementation status: sufficient (high-gain but mixed close-family context). Closure justification status: now sufficient for neutral aromatic vs ICT under a best-available standard because the last internal ambiguity (torsion-induced dark-lowest-state) has been removed by the S0-optimized torsion parse.

Chosen next action: finalize_best_available, because (i) verifier supplementation is already sufficient, (ii) the targeted pairwise discriminator task has now directly resolved the main internal conflict, and (iii) remaining missing evidence (CT-number/Δμ/solvatochromism) is not currently obtainable with the demonstrated low-cost internal routes.

- hypothesis_uncertainty_note: Residual uncertainty is primarily epistemic: the workflow still lacks decisive CT metrics (CT-number, NTO hole/electron separation, Δμ) and experimental solvatochromism, so a borderline LE/ICT mixture cannot be ruled out in principle. Nevertheless, the robust bright lowest S1 across relaxed conformers and S0-optimized torsion snapshots makes an LE/neutral-aromatic dominant assignment the best-available label.

- final_hypothesis_rationale: Best-available mechanism label: neutral aromatic. The molecule is a neutral, rotor-rich multi-aryl ethylene scaffold (RIM-compatible), and across (i) a 6-member relaxed conformer bundle and (ii) S0-optimized torsion snapshots along a conjugation-relevant aryl–vinyl dihedral, the lowest excited state remains consistently the first bright state with high oscillator strength (S1 f≈0.43–0.47) and minimal sensitivity to twisting. This behavior is most consistent with a robust LE π–π* manifold typical of neutral multi-aryl AIEgens rather than a dominant ICT/TICT state that would be expected to show stronger geometry dependence and/or low-lying dark CT competition.

- capability_assessment: Microscopic: strong for generating/paring vertical excited-state manifolds across conformers and torsion snapshots and extracting energies/oscillator strengths plus dominant transition surrogates. Persistent limitation: low-cost routes did not provide decisive CT diagnostics (NTO localization, CT-number, e–h separation/overlap, Δμ). Verifier: provided sufficient close-family context but no exact-compound hit; emphasized solvatochromism/CT-number as decisive for LE vs ICT.
